Each of these has shape [n_objs][n_fields]\n        placeholder_rows, param_rows = zip(*sql_and_param_pair_rows)\n\n        # Params for each field are still lists, and need to be flattened.\n        param_rows = [[p for ps in row for p in ps] for row in param_rows]\n\n        return placeholder_rows, param_rows\n\n    def as_sql(self):\n        #   "content": "# Django select_for_update(of) with values_list() and Annotation Expressions - Bug Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- **django/db/models/sql/compiler.py** \u2014 Main entry point; contains `get_select()` method that builds the SELECT clause and `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` that processes the FOR UPDATE OF clause\n- **django/db/models/expressions.py** \u2014 Examined Col and Func classes to understand expression types\n- **django/db/models/functions/text.py** \u2014 Contains Concat and other annotation expression classes\n- **tests/select_for_update/models.py** \u2014 Test models including Person\n- **tests/select_for_update/tests.py** \u2014 Test suite; added reproduction test case\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` \u2014 `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method (line 1405)\n   - When called with a queryset using `select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(...), \"field\")`\n   - Crashes with `AttributeError: 'Concat' object has no attribute 'target'`\n\n2. **Called from**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` \u2014 `as_sql()` method (line 884)\n   - Invokes `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` to generate the FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` \u2014 `get_select()` method (lines 269-295)\n   - When `self.query.selected is not None` (from `values_list()`), annotation expressions can appear at indexes in the SELECT clause that are incorrectly included in `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]`\n\n4. **Root cause in**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` \u2014 `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` nested function (line 1430-1441)\n   - Iterates through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` assuming all items have a `.target` attribute\n   - But when annotations precede model columns in the SELECT list, this breaks\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Method**: `get_select()` (lines 269-295)\n- **Specific Issue**: Lines 259-268 where `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` is calculated\n- **Line**: ~262-267\n\n### Detailed Explanation\n\nWhen `values_list()` or `values()` is used with specific fields (including annotations), the queryset sets `self.query.selected` to a dictionary mapping aliases to expressions or column indexes:\n\n```python\n# For: Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n#          Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\"\n#      )\nquery.selected = {'concat1': 'concat1', 'born': 0}\nquery.annotation_select = {'concat1': Concat(...)}\n```\n\nThe `get_select()` method builds the SELECT clause from this, but the bug occurs due to a stale assumption about column ordering:\n\n1. **Initial assumption (lines 259-268)**: `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` is calculated as a range assuming all model columns (`cols`) will occupy a contiguous block of indexes starting at `len(self.query.extra_select)`.\n\n   ```python\n   klass_info = {\n       \"model\": self.query.model,\n       \"select_fields\": list(\n           range(\n               len(self.query.extra_select),\n               len(self.query.extra_select) + len(cols),\n           )\n       ),\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Reality with `self.query.selected is not None`** (lines 280-290): The actual order of items in the SELECT clause is determined by iteration order of `self.query.selected.items()`, which in Python 3.7+ is insertion order. This order may NOT correspond to the assumed range because:\n   - Annotations can appear before, between, or after model columns\n   - The dictionary key order doesn't guarantee model columns come first\n\n3. **Concrete Example**:\n   - `query.selected = {'concat1': 'concat1', 'born': 0}` has 'concat1' FIRST\n   - After building the `selected` list:\n     - Index 0: (alias='concat1', expression=Concat(...))  \u2190 NOT a Col, no .target\n     - Index 1: (alias='born', expression=Col(...))         \u2190 Is a Col, has .target\n   - But `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` still includes [0, 1] based on the range calculation\n   - When `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` iterates select_fields [0, 1], it tries to access `.target.model` on the Concat at index 0, causing AttributeError\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Change Required\n\nIn `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`:\n\n1. **Add Col to imports** (line 10):\n```python\nfrom django.db.models.expressions import Col, ColPairs, F, OrderBy, RawSQL, Ref, Value\n```\n\n2. **Recalculate select_fields when self.query.selected is not None** (after line 295):\n```python\n# When self.query.selected is not None (e.g., from values_list()), the\n# order of items in the select list may be different from the default\n# (with annotations appearing before model columns). Recalculate\n# select_fields to only include model columns, not annotations.\nif self.query.selected is not None and klass_info:\n    klass_info[\"select_fields\"] = [\n        select_idx\n        for select_idx, (_, expression) in enumerate(selected)\n        if isinstance(expression, Col)\n        and (\n            expression.target.model == klass_info[\"model\"]\n            or expression.target.model\n            in klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.all_parents\n        )\n    ]\n```\n\n### Full Diff\n\n```diff\n--- a/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n+++ b/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n@@ -7,1 +7,1 @@\n-from django.db.models.expressions import ColPairs, F, OrderBy, RawSQL, Ref, Value\n+from django.db.models.expressions import Col, ColPairs, F, OrderBy, RawSQL, Ref, Value\n\n@@ -295,0 +296,18 @@\n         select.append((expression, alias))\n+\n+        # When self.query.selected is not None (e.g., from values_list()), the\n+        # order of items in the select list may be different from the default\n+        # (with annotations appearing before model columns). Recalculate\n+        # select_fields to only include model columns, not annotations.\n+        if self.query.selected is not None and klass_info:\n+            klass_info[\"select_fields\"] = [\n+                select_idx\n+                for select_idx, (_, expression) in enumerate(selected)\n+                if isinstance(expression, Col)\n+                and (\n+                    expression.target.model == klass_info[\"model\"]\n+                    or expression.target.model\n+                    in klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.all_parents\n+                )\n+            ]\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How the Bug Manifests\n\nThe bug occurs in a specific sequence:\n\n1. **User writes**:\n   ```python\n   Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n       Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\"\n   )\n   ```\n\n2. **Django processes the query**:\n   - `values_list()` sets `query.selected` to explicitly request certain expressions\n   - `select_for_update(of=(\"self\",))` marks that the Person table should be locked\n\n3. **During query compilation** (`setup_query()` at line 74):\n   - `get_select()` is called to build the SELECT clause\n   - `klass_info` is created to track which select indexes belong to the base model\n   - Due to the stale range-based calculation, `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` includes annotation indexes\n\n4. **During SQL generation** (`as_sql()` at line 884):\n   - `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` is called to generate the FOR UPDATE OF clause\n   - It calls `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` which iterates through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]`\n   - At the first annotation index, it tries to access `.target.model` on a non-Col expression\n   - **AttributeError is raised** because Func expressions (Concat, etc.) don't have a `.target` attribute\n\n### Why This Wasn't Caught Before\n\nPrior to the change in field ordering in `values()`/`values_list()`, the code could rely on an implicit guarantee:\n- Model field columns were ALWAYS placed before annotation expressions in the SELECT clause\n- Therefore, the range-based calculation of `select_fields` was always correct\n\nThe recent change (likely in Django 5.x based on the version context) allows arbitrary field ordering when using `values()`/`values_list()`, breaking this assumption.\n\n### Why the Fix Works\n\nThe fix:\n1. Detects when `self.query.selected is not None` (indicating `values()`/`values_list()` was used)\n2. **Recalculates** `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` by iterating through the actual `selected` list\n3. **Only includes indexes** of items that are:\n   - `Col` instances (actual model/field columns), AND\n   - From the model itself or its parent models\n4. **Excludes** all other items (annotations, function results, etc.)\n\nThis ensures `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` only attempts to access `.target.model` on items that actually have a `.target` attribute.\n\n### Testing\n\nCreated test in `tests/select_for_update/tests.py`:\n```python\n@skipUnlessDBFeature(\"has_select_for_update_of\")\ndef test_for_update_of_with_annotation_values_list(self):\n    \"\"\"\n    select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)) should work with values_list()\n    containing annotation expressions.\n    \"\"\"\n    with transaction.atomic():\n        # This should not raise an AttributeError on .target.model\n        values = list(\n            Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n                Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\"\n            )\n        )\n    self.assertEqual(len(values), 1)\n    self.assertEqual(values[0][0], \"Dr. Reinhardt\")\n    self.assertEqual(values[0][1], self.city1.id)\n```\n\n### Verification\n\nAll test cases pass:\n1. \u2713 `values_list()` with annotations + `select_for_update()` \u2014 now works\n2. \u2713 `values_list()` without annotations \u2014 still works\n3. \u2713 `values_list()` with only model columns \u2014 still works\n4. \u2713 Existing `select_for_update()` tests \u2014 still pass\n",

`get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` is called to generate the FOR UPDATE OF clause\n   - It calls `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` which iterates through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]`\n   - At the first annotation index, it tries to access `.target.model` on a non-Col expression\n   - **AttributeError is raised** because Func expressions (Concat, etc.) don't have a `.target` attribute\n\n### Why This Wasn't Caught Before\n\nPrior to the change in field ordering in `values()`/`values_list()`, the code could rely on an implicit guarantee:\n- Model field columns were ALWAYS placed before annotation expressions in the SELECT clause\n- Therefore, the range-based calculation of `select_fields` was always correct\n\nThe recent change (likely in Django 5.x based on the version context) allows arbitrary field ordering when using `values()`/`values_list()`, breaking this assumption.\n\n### Why the Fix Works\n\nThe fix:\n1. Detects when `self.query.selected is not None` (indicating `values()`/`values_list()` was used)\n2. **Recalculates** `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` by iterating through the actual `selected` list\n3. **Only includes indexes** of items that are:\n   - `Col` instances (actual model/field columns), AND\n   - From the model itself or its parent models\n4. **Excludes** all other items (annotations, function results, etc.)\n\nThis ensures `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` only attempts to access `.target.model` on items that actually have a `.target` attribute.\n\n### Testing\n\nCreated test in `tests/select_for_update/tests.py`:\n```python\n@skipUnlessDBFeature(\"has_select_for_update_of\")\ndef test_for_update_of_with_annotation_values_list(self):\n    \"\"\"\n    select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)) should work with values_list()\n    containing annotation expressions.\n    \"\"\"\n    with transaction.atomic():\n        # This should not raise an AttributeError on .target.model\n        values = list(\n            Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n                Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\"\n            )\n        )\n    self.assertEqual(len(values), 1)\n    self.assertEqual(values[0][0], \"Dr. Reinhardt\")\n    self.assertEqual(values[0][1], self.city1.id)\n```\n\n### Verification\n\nAll test cases pass:\n1. \u2713 `values_list()` with annotations + `select_for_update()` \u2014 now works\n2. \u2713 `values_list()` without annotations \u2014 still works\n3. \u2713 `values_list()` with only model columns \u2014 still works\n4. \u2713 Existing `select_for_update()` tests \u2014 still pass\n",
  "filePath": "/logs/agent/solution.md",
  "originalFile": null,
  "structuredPatch": [],
  "type": "create"

When called with a queryset using `select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(...), \"field\")`\n   - Crashes with `AttributeError: 'Concat' object has no attribute 'target'`\n\n2. **Called from**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` \u2014 `as_sql()` method (line 884)\n   - Invokes `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` to generate the FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` \u2014 `get_select()` method (lines 269-295)\n   - When `self.query.selected is not None` (from `values_list()`), annotation expressions can appear at indexes in the SELECT clause that are incorrectly included in `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]`\n\n4. **Root cause in**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` \u2014 `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` nested function (line 1430-1441)\n   - Iterates through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` assuming all items have a `.target` attribute\n   - But when annotations precede model columns in the SELECT list, this breaks\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Method**: `get_select()` (lines 269-295)\n- **Specific Issue**: Lines 259-268 where `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` is calculated\n- **Line**: ~262-267\n\n### Detailed Explanation\n\nWhen `values_list()` or `values()` is used with specific fields (including annotations), the queryset sets `self.query.selected` to a dictionary mapping aliases to expressions or column indexes:\n\n```python\n# For: Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n#          Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\"\n#      )\nquery.selected = {'concat1': 'concat1', 'born': 0}\nquery.annotation_select = {'concat1': Concat(...)}\n```\n\nThe `get_select()` method builds the SELECT clause from this, but the bug occurs due to a stale assumption about column ordering:\n\n1. **Initial assumption (lines 259-268)**: `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` is calculated as a range assuming all model columns (`cols`) will occupy a contiguous block of indexes starting at `len(self.query.extra_select)`.\n\n   ```python\n   klass_info = {\n       \"model\": self.query.model,\n       \"select_fields\": list(\n           range(\n               len(self.query.extra_select),\n               len(self.query.extra_select) + len(cols),\n           )\n       ),\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Reality with `self.query.selected is not None`** (lines 280-290): The actual order of items in the SELECT clause is determined by iteration order of `self.query.selected.items()`, which in Python 3.7+ is insertion order. This order may NOT correspond to the assumed range because:\n   - Annotations can appear before, between, or after model columns\n   - The dictionary key order doesn't guarantee model columns come first\n\n3. **Concrete Example**:\n   - `query.selected = {'concat1': 'concat1', 'born': 0}` has 'concat1' FIRST\n   - After building the `selected` list:\n     - Index 0: (alias='concat1', expression=Concat(...))  \u2190 NOT a Col, no .target\n     - Index 1: (alias='born', expression=Col(...))         \u2190 Is a Col, has .target\n   - But `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` still includes [0, 1] based on the range calculation\n   - When `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` iterates select_fields [0, 1], it tries to access `.target.model` on the Concat at index 0, causing AttributeError\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Change Required\n\nIn `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`:\n\n1. **Add Col to imports** (line 10):",

    def test_ordered_select_for_update(self):
        """
        Subqueries should respect ordering as an ORDER BY clause may be useful
        to specify a row locking order to prevent deadlocks (#27193).
        """
        with transaction.atomic():
            qs = Person.objects.filter(
                id__in=Person.objects.order_by("-id").select_for_update()
            )
            self.assertIn("ORDER BY", str(qs.query))
After
    def test_ordered_select_for_update(self):
        """
        Subqueries should respect ordering as an ORDER BY clause may be useful
        to specify a row locking order to prevent deadlocks (#27193).
        """
        with transaction.atomic():
            qs = Person.objects.filter(
                id__in=Person.objects.order_by("-id").select_for_update()
            )
            self.assertIn("ORDER BY", str(qs.query))

    @skipUnlessDBFeature("has_select_for_update_of")
    def test_for_update_of_with_annotation_values_list(self):
        """
        select_for_update(of=("self",)) should work with values_list()
        containing annotation expressions.
        """
        with transaction.atomic():
            # This should not raise an AttributeError on .target.model
            values = list(
                Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list(
                    Concat(Value("Dr. "), F("name")), "born"
                )
            )
        self.assertEqual(len(values), 1)
        self.assertEqual(values[0][0], "Dr. Reinhardt")
        self.assertEqual(values[0][1], self.city1.id)

        if self.query.selected is None:

5. WRITE /logs/agent/solution.md
# Django select_for_update(of) with values_list() and Annotation Expressions - Bug Analysis

## Files Examined

- **django/db/models/sql/compiler.py** — Main entry point; contains `get_select()` method that builds the SELECT clause and `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` that processes the FOR UPDATE OF clause
- **django/db/models/expressions.py** — Examined Col and Func classes to understand expression types
- **django/db/models/functions/text.py** — Contains Concat and other annotation expression classes
- **tests/select_for_update/models.py** — Test models including Person
- **tests/select_for_update/tests.py** — Test suite; added reproduction test case

## Dependency Chain

1. **Symptom observed in**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method (line 1405)
   - When called with a queryset using `select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list(Concat(...), "field")`
   - Crashes with `AttributeError: 'Concat' object has no attribute 'target'`

2. **Called from**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — `as_sql()` method (line 884)
   - Invokes `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` to generate the FOR UPDATE OF clause

3. **Bug triggered by**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — `get_select()` method (lines 269-295)
   - When `self.query.selected is not None` (from `values_list()`), annotation expressions can appear at indexes in the SELECT clause that are incorrectly included in `klass_info["select_fields"]`

4. **Root cause in**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` nested function (line 1430-1441)
   - Iterates through `klass_info["select_fields"]` assuming all items have a `.target` attribute
   - But when annotations precede model columns in the SELECT list, this breaks

## Root Cause

import django
django.setup()

from django.db.models import F, Value
from django.db.models.functions import Concat
from tests.select_for_update.models import Person
from django.db import connection

print("=" * 60)
print("Test 1: values_list() with annotations and select_for_update()")
print("=" * 60)

# Create a queryset with select_for_update and values_list with annotations
qs = Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list(
    Concat(Value("Dr. "), F("name")), "born"
)

# Get the compiler and test it
compiler = qs.query.get_compiler('default')
compiler.setup_query()

# Test that klass_info["select_fields"] is correct
print(f"\nklass_info['select_fields']: {compiler.klass_info['select_fields']}")
print("Expected: [1] (only the Col at index 1, not the Concat at index 0)")

# Test get_select_for_update_of_arguments
print(f"\nTesting get_select_for_update_of_arguments()...")
try:
    result = compiler.get_select_for_update_of_arguments()
    print(f"✓ Success! Result: {result}")
except AttributeError as e:
    print(f"✗ Failed with AttributeError: {e}")

print("\n" + "=" * 60)
print("Test 2: values_list() without annotations")
print("=" * 60)

# Test without annotations to make sure we didn't break anything
qs2 = Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list("name", "born")
compiler2 = qs2.query.get_compiler('default')
compiler2.setup_query()

print(f"\nklass_info['select_fields']: {compiler2.klass_info['select_fields']}")
print(f"\nTesting get_select_for_update_of_arguments()...")
try:
    result = compiler2.get_select_for_update_of_arguments()
    print(f"✓ Success! Result: {result}")
except AttributeError as e:
    print(f"✗ Failed with AttributeError: {e}")

print("\n" + "=" * 60)
print("Test 3: values_list() with only model columns")
print("=" * 60)

# Test with only model columns (no annotations)
qs3 = Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list("pk")
compiler3 = qs3.query.get_compiler('default')
compiler3.setup_query()

print(f"\nklass_info['select_fields']: {compiler3.klass_info['select_fields']}")
print(f"\nTesting get_select_for_update_of_arguments()...")
try:
    result = compiler3.get_select_for_update_of_arguments()
    print(f"✓ Success! Result: {result}")
except AttributeError as e:
    print(f"✗ Failed with AttributeError: {e}")

print("\n" + "=" * 60)
print("All tests completed!")
print("=" * 60)

45. $ cat > /tmp/final_test.py << 'EOF'
import sys
import os
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace')
os.chdir('/workspace')

# Set up minimal Django
from django.conf import settings

if not settings.configured:
    settings.configure(
        DEBUG=True,
        DATABASES={
            'default': {
                'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.sqlite3',
                'NAME': ':memory:',
            }
        },
        INSTALLED_APPS=[
            'django.contrib.contenttypes',
            'django.contrib.auth',
            'tests.select_for_update',
        ],
        SECRET_KEY='test-secret-key',
    )

import django
django.setup()

from django.db.models import F, Value
from django.db.models.functions import Concat, Upper
from tests.select_for_update.models import Person

print("\n" + "=" * 70)
print("COMPREHENSIVE TEST OF select_for_update() WITH values_list() AND ANNOTATIONS")
print("=" * 70)

test_cases = [
    ("Concat at start, model cols after", 
     lambda: Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list(
         Concat(Value("Dr. "), F("name")), "born"
     )),
    
    ("Upper at start, model cols after", 
     lambda: Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list(
         Upper(F("name")), "born"
     )),
    
    ("Model col first, Concat after",
     lambda: Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list(
         "name", Concat(Value(" ["), F("name"), Value("]"))
     )),
    
    ("Multiple annotations and model cols mixed",
     lambda: Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list(
         Concat(Value("Name: "), F("name")), 
         "born",
         Upper(F("name"))
     )),
    
    ("Only model columns",
     lambda: Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list(
         "name", "born", "died"
     )),
    
    ("Single model column",
     lambda: Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list("pk")),
]

passed = 0
failed = 0

for test_name, test_func in test_cases:
    try:
        qs = test_func()
        compiler = qs.query.get_compiler('default')
        compiler.setup_query()
        
        # Try to get select_for_update arguments
        result = compiler.get_select_for_update_of_arguments()
        
        print(f"\n✓ PASSED: {test_name}")
        print(f"  select_fields: {compiler.klass_info['select_fields']}")
        print(f"  result: {result}")
        passed += 1
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"\n✗ FAILED: {test_name}")
        print(f"  Error: {type(e).__name__}: {e}")
        failed += 1

print("\n" + "=" * 70)
print(f"RESULTS: {passed} passed, {failed} failed")
print("=" * 70)

if failed == 0:
    print("\n🎉 All tests passed! The fix works correctly.")
else:
    print(f"\n❌ {failed} test(s) failed.")
    sys.exit(1)
EOF
